                            <div class="player-info-box-header team-reds"><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Joey Votto</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team"><a href="/teams/reds">Cincinnati Reds</a></div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 34</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: L/R</div>

        <div class="player-info-box-pos">1B</div></div>

                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>9/10/1983 (34 y, 6 m)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=4314&position=1B#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2002 June Amateur Draft - Round: 2, Pick: 3, Overall: 44, Team: Cincinnati Reds</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=4314&position=1B#contract" >$225M / 10 Years (2014 - 2023) + 1 Option Years</a>

(9/28/2017)</div></td></tr>

        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b> In his second full season, Joey Votto posted the fourth-highest wOBA in baseball and, once adjusted for park and league, ended up fifth on that list.  He had his highest BB/K ratio of his career and an extremely high BABIP of .372.  Really the only smudge on his 2009 season was the fact that he missed time due to flu/inner ear/stress/depression-related ailments that kept him out some of May and most of June.<br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b> Most would point to Votto’s BABIP of .372 and say he’s due for a lot of regression, at least when it comes to batting average.  However, our very own Dave Allen’s research suggests that because of his solid power to all fields, coupled with his very low pop-up rates, that it’s reasonable for Votto’s BABIP to remain high, though not quite as high.  With this in mind, a BABIP between .340 and .350 would not be unreasonable to expect, which would certainly keep his batting average above .300.   If you miss out on the bigger name first basemen, Votto is certainly a viable alternative.  When 2010 is all said and done, he should be a top-ten first baseman, with a chance to sneak into the seventh spot.  Anything higher than that would be an unexpected, though not unwelcome, bonus for those not looking to pay top dollar at first base.  (David Appelman)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The fact that Votto managed to surpass such players as Albert Pujols and Carlos Gonzalez for his first career MVP award reflects just how impressive his numbers were. In case you still need convincing, Votto posted a .324/.424/.600 line behind a 14% BB rate and a massive .276 ISO last season, good for a .439 wOBA and 7.4 WAR. Votto was helped a bit by a .361 BABIP, but his numbers to date suggest that he could be one of those special hitters who repeatedly posts such numbers. In 1282 balls in play, he has a .353 career BABIP. Due to the variable nature of the statistic, we still can't conclusively say that he will maintain that mark. However, he's a good bet for at least an above-average BABIP, and with the rest of his skill set, he can bring the total fantasy package. Votto is a legitimate No. 2 on draft boards this summer, as another .320-35-100 season would be no surprise at all out of the Reds' young superstar. (Jack Moore)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Votto won his first MVP in impressive fashion. Regression could lower his batting average, but he's still among the best players in the league, well worth a first-round pick.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Was that a bad year? Votto came within one home run of 30 and two stolen bases of ten. He hit over .300 once again, with great patience and defense. With his plate discipline and batted ball mix, the batting average is sustainable going forward. Even if the stolen bases continue to decline, he'll still have all those runs and RBI to drool over. He seems immune to the bad year, even if he doesn't quite have Albert Pujols power. Where you take him just depends on how much you want to pay for a stud player that doesn't play a premium position. But in NL-only leagues, remember that two studs left the league this year, making Votto even more special. (Eno Sarris)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>If that was a bad year from Joey Votto, then it's probably a good idea to keep signing up for more of that production going forward. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Votto defines the elite first baseman, particular in a National League depleted by last year's defections from Prince Fielder and Albert Pujols. A .337 average and .474 (!) OBP in 2012 signal that he remains a great pick in leagues using either rate stat. His 14 home runs may be a discouraging total, but his power just wasn't there after his return from a July meniscus injury. After an offseason of recovery, expect Votto to return at 100 percent for his age-29 season, a four-category monster at first base once again. (Jack Moore)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Votto is probably the best bet out there in both offensive rate stats (batting average and on-base percentage). His power suffered in the wake of a July meniscus injury, but expect Votto to put it behind him for 2013. Draft as an elite player.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>A $15 first baseman -- seventh-best at the position according to our end-of-season rankings -- is probably not what people had in mind when they drafted Joey Votto last March. And the thing that might hurt just a little bit for a fantasy player that's also well-versed in real-life value is the fact that his missing RBI probably had a lot to do with that shortcoming. 73 RBI is about twenty short of a full stack for an elite first baseman in the fantasy game. If you're in an on-base percentage league, you don't care. His .435 OBP led baseball again last year, and that probably floated some shortcomings in other departments. But batting-average league players were left with a decent batting average, good runs scored, a few stolen bases, and not much more. The thing is, there's not much of a reason to believe he's going to do much more. His power peripherals have been reasonably steady for three years now, and it's part of his <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/joey-votto-on-hitting/">self-declared approach at the plate</a>. So, pay for a .300 batting average (or a .400+ OBP), mid-twenties homers, and hope the Reds offense provides him more RBI opportunities in 2014. Just don't expect 2010 to come back. (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/enosarris">Eno Sarris</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Joey Votto is not your monkey. His current approach is worth too much to his real-life team for him to to start swinging harder, or swinging at worse pitches, just because you want more RBI and homerz. That doesn't mean he's not a great player. In real life.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>In 2014, Joey Votto disappointed for the first time in his career. Even in his injury-shortened 2012, he was still the most productive hitter in baseball while he played. But Votto's always-elite average dipped considerably and his power took a hit, too, as he dealt with a quad injuries to both legs throughout the season. The low batting average is almost unexplainable, as nothing changed in his fantastic walk, strikeout, and line drive rates, and it's almost impossible to see him hitting anywhere near .260 again. He might not be much more than 20 homer guy at this point in his career, but that's fine considering what he does in other areas. And if you're in a league where OBP matters, Votto could arguably still be a top-10 first baseman, as he had an incredible .390 on-base percentage in the "worst" season of his career last year. In non-OBP leagues, he becomes a still-solid guy who's better in real life than fantasy. Knee surgery and double quad injuries within the last three years are worrisome, as is the drop in production. But at 31, it's far too early to even begin writing Votto off as some frustrated owners wanted to last year, as he's still one of the most pure all-around hitters in baseball. (August Fagerstrom)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Votto was a disappointment to fantasy owners who wasted a high draft pick on him in 2014, but his approach leaves him nearly immune to prolonged slumps and we're still talking about a guy with a .390 OBP in a "disappointing season." With a high floor and still tremendous upside, I wouldn't sleep on Joey Votto in 2015, especially in OBP leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Coming off the best season of his career, it's easy to forget Joey Votto is 32 now. That, and a batting average on balls in play near .400, might give you pause about re-upping with the Reds' first baseman in the coming season. Except that Votto has tailored his approach to having a high BABIP, and also towards aging well. He's not going to reach, he's not dependent on making contact outside the zone, and his power comes naturally from his line drive approach. He knows the strike zone and can cover the entire plate, and this year added a wrinkle -- he can take the extreme inside pitch the other way, over the shortstop's head. A swing tailored to take the outside pitch right-center with power, that can now cover the inside part of the plate? Baseball's sweetest swing should be able to keep producing great batting averages and on-base percentages in the near future. Power, and health, are the only question marks, but a renewed emphasis on fitness give us hope that he'll be good, there too. Still all systems go here. (Eno Sarris)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The pants tell the story -- Votto's leaner physique should help him stay healthier in the future. That means more line drives, sprayed all over the field, and value for your fantasy team. After the two young studs at his position are gone, consider Votto the best veteran.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Remember when Votto concluded the month of May with just a .213 batting average, driven by a suppressed .254 BABIP? Probably not. Because his next four months more than made up for the slow start, as he batted a crazy .378, thanks to a .409 BABIP, and finished the year generally in line with his 2015 season. Heading into his age 33 season, we would expect to find some signs of skill deterioration, but he just posted the second lowest strikeout rate of his career, the second highest HR/FB rate of his career, and continues to maintain a pristine batted ball profile chock full of line drives and absent of pop-ups. I can't believe those bonus steals will continue to come and I wouldn't bank on another 20%+ HR/FB rate. However, he remains solid as a rock with a beautiful overall set of skills. (<a href="http://www.projectingx.com/" target="_blank">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Feel free to stare at Votto's immaculate batted ball profile, as it drives that inflated BABIP and allows him to hit well over .300 season after season. Even heading into his age 33 season, there are no signs of decline, so he should once again be a power source and strong batting average contributor.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
